velitrae in the volscian country and have be leave without a protector by the death of he father octavius he be bring up in the house of he mother and she husband lucius philippus but on attain maturity spend he time with caesar the latter who be childless base great hope upon he and be devote to he intend to leave he as successor to he name authority and supremacy he be influence largely by attium 's explicit affirmation that the youth have be engender by apollo while sleep once in he temple she say she think she have intercourse with a serpent and through this circumstance at the end of the allotted time bear a son before he come to the light of day she see in a dream she womb lift to the heaven and spread out over all the earth and the same night octavius think the sun rise from she vagina hardly have the child be bear when nigidius figulus a senator straightway prophesy for he sole command of the realm -lrb- 2 -rrb- he could distinguish most accurately of he contemporary the order of the firmament and the mutation of the star what they accomplish by separation and what by conjunction in they association and retirement and for this reason have incur the charge of practice some kind of forbid pursuit he accordingly meet on that occasion octavius who be somewhat tardy in reach the senate on account of the birth of the child -- there happen to be a meeting of the senate that day -- and ask he why he be late on learn the cause he cry out : you have beget a master over we -lrb- 3 -rrb- at that octavius be alarm and wish to destroy the infant but nigidius restrain he say that it be impossible for it to suffer any such fate -lrb- -2 - -rrb- this be the conversation at that time while the boy be grow up in the country a eagle snatch from he hand a loaf of bread and after soar aloft fly down and give it back to he -lrb- 4 -rrb- when he be a lad and staying in rome cicero dream that the boy be let down by golden chain to the summit of the capitol and receive a whip from jupiter -lrb- 5 -rrb- he do not know who the youth be but meet he the next day on the capitol itself he recognize he and tell the vision to the bystander catulus who have likewise never see octavius beheld in a vision all the noble child on the capitol at the termination of a solemn procession to jupiter and in the course of the ceremony the god cast what look like a image of rome into that child 's lap startle at this he go up into the capitol to offer prayer to the god and finding there octavius who have ascend the hill for some other reason he compare he appearance with the dream and be satisfy of the truth of the vision when later he have become a young man and be about to reach maturity he be put on the dress of a adult when he tunic be rent on both side from he shoulder and fall to he foot this event of itself not only have no significance as forecasting any good fortune but displeased the spectator considerably because it have happen in he first put on the garb of a man : it occur to octavius to say : i shall put the whole senatorial dignity beneath my foot and the outcome prove in accordance with he word caesar found great hope upon he as a result of this introduce he into the class of patrician and train he for rulership in everything that be proper to come to the notice of one destine to control so great a power well and worthily he educate he with care the youth be train in oratorical speech not only in the latin but in this language -lrb- greek -rrb- labor persistently in military campaign and receive minute instruction in politics and the science of government -lrb- -3 - -rrb- now this octavius chance at the time that caesar be murder to be in apollonium near the ionic gulf pursue he education he have be send thither in advance to look after he patron 's intended campaign against the parthian when he learn of the event he be naturally grieve but do not dare at once to take any radical measure he have not yet hear that he have be make caesar 's son or heir and moreover the first news he receive be to the effect that the people be of one mind in the affair when however he have cross to brundusium and have be inform about the will and the people 's second thought he make no delay particularly because he have considerable money and numerous soldier who have be send on under he charge but he immediately assume the name of caesar succeed to he estate and begin to busy himself with the situation -lrb- -4 - -rrb- at the time he seem to some to have act recklessly and daringly in this but later as a result of he good fortune and the success he achieve he acquire a reputation for bravery in many instance in history man who be wrong in undertake some project have be fame for wisdom because they prove fortunate in it : other who use the best possible judgment have have to stand a charge of folly because they do not attain they end he too act in a blundering and dangerous way he be only just past boyhood -- eighteen year of age -- and see that the succession to the inheritance and the family be sure to provoke jealousy and censure : yet he start in pursuit of object that have lead to caesar 's murder and no punishment befall he and he fear neither the assassin nor lepidus and antony yet he be not think to have plan poorly because he become successful heaven however indicate not obscurely all the upheaval that would result from it as he be enter rome a great variegated iris surround the whole sun -lrb- -5 - -rrb- in this way he that be formerly call octavius but already at this time caesar and subsequently augustus take charge of affair and settle they and bring they to a successful close more vigourously than any mature man more prudently than any graybeard first he enter the city as if for the sole purpose of succeed to the inheritance and as a private citizen with only a few attendant without any ostentation still later he do not utter any threat against any one nor show that he be displeased at what have occur and would take vengeance for it so far from demand of antony any of the money that he have previously plunder he actually pay court to he although he be insult and wrong by he among the other injury that antony do he by both word and deed be he action when the lex curia be propose accord to which the transfer of octavius into caesar 's family be to take place : antony himself of course be active to have it pass but through some tribune he secure its postponement in order that the young man be not yet caesar 's child accord to law might not meddle with the property and might be weaker in all other way -lrb- -6 - -rrb- caesar be restive under this treatment but as he be unable to speak he mind freely he bear it until he have win over the crowd by whose member he understand he father have be raise to honor he know that they be angry at the latter 's death and hope they would be enthusiastic over he as he son and perceive that they hate antony on account of he have be master of the horse and also for he failure to punish the murderer hence he undertake to become tribune as a start point for popular leadership and to secure the power that would result from it and he accordingly become a candidate for the place of cinna which be vacant though hinder by antony 's clique he do not desist and after use persuasion upon tiberius cannutius a tribune he be by he bring before the populace he take as a excuse the gift bequeath by caesar and in he speech touch upon all the important point promise that he would discharge this debt at once and give they cause to hope for much besides after this come the festival appoint in honor of the completion of the temple of venus which some while caesar be alive have promise to celebrate but be now hold in slight regard as they do the horse-race connect with the parilium -lrb- 6 -rrb- and to win the favor of the populace he provide for it at he private expense on the ground that it concern he because of he family at this time out of fear of antony he bring into the theater neither caesar 's gilded chair nor he crown set with precious stone though it be permit by decree -lrb- -7 - -rrb- when however a certain star through all those day appear in the north toward evening some call it a comet and say that it indicate the usual occurrence but the majority instead of believe this ascribe it to caesar interpret it to mean that he have become a god and have be include in the number of the star then octavius take courage and set up in the temple of venus a bronze statue of he with a star above he head through fear of the populace no one prevent this and then at last some of the earlier decree in regard to honor to caesar be put into effect they call one of the month July after he and in the course of certain triumphal religious festival they sacrifice during one special day in memory of he name for these reason the soldier also and particularly since some of they receive largess of money readily take the side of caesar rumor accordingly go abroad and it seem likely that something unusual would take place this idea gain most headway for the reason that when octavius be somewhat anxious to show himself in court in a elevated and conspicuous place as he have be wont to do in he father 's lifetime antony would not allow it but have he lictor drag he down and drive he out -lrb- -8 - -rrb- all be exceedingly vexed and especially because caesar with a view to cast odium upon he rival and arouse the multitude would no longer even frequent the forum so antony become terrify and in conversation with the bystander one day remark that he harbor no anger against caesar but on the contrary owe he affection and feel inclined to dispel the entire cloud of suspicion the statement be report to the other they hold a conference and some thought they have become reconcile as a fact they understand each other 's disposition accurately and think it inopportune at that time to put they to the test they come to term by make a few mutual concession for some day they be quiet then they begin to suspect each other afresh as a result of either some really hostile action or some false report of hostility -- as regularly happen under such condition -- and be again at variance when man become reconcile after a great enmity they be suspicious of many act that contain no malice and of many chance occurrence in brief they regard everything in the light of they former hostility as do on purpose and for a evil end while they be in this condition those who stand on neutral ground aggravate the trouble irritate they still more by bear report to and fro under the pretence of devotion there be a very large element which be anxious to see all those who have power at variance with one another -- a element which consequently take delight in they enmity and join in plot against they and the party which have previously suffer from calumny be very easy to deceive with word adapt to the purpose by a band of friend whose attachment be not under suspicion this also account for the fact that these man who do not trust each other previously become now even more estrange -lrb- -9 - -rrb- antony see that caesar be gain ground attempt to attract the populace by various bait to see if he could detach the people from he rival and number they among he own force hence through lucius antonius he brother who be tribune he introduce a measure that considerable land be open for settlement among the parcel be the region of the pontine marsh which he state have already be fill and be capable of cultivation the three antonius who be brother all hold office at the same time marcus be consul lucius tribune and gaius praetor therefore they could very easily remove those who be temporarily ruler of they ally and subject -lrb- except the majority of the assassin and some other whom they regard as loyal -rrb- and choose other in place of they : they could also grant some the right to hold office for a unusually long term contrary to the law establish by caesar also macedonium which fall to marcus by lot be appropriate by he brother gaius but marcus himself with the legion previously despatch into apollonium lay claim to gaul on this side of the alp to which decimus brutus have be assign the reason be that it seem to be very strong in resource of soldier and money after these measure have be pass the immunity grant to sextus pompey by caesar as to all the rest be confirm : he have already considerable influence it be further resolve that whatever money of silver or gold the public treasury have take from he ancestral estate should be restore as for the land belong to it antony hold the most of they and make no restoration -lrb- -10 - -rrb- this be the business in which they be engage but i shall now go on to describe how sextus have fare when he have flee from corduba he first come to lacetanium and conceal himself there he be pursue to be sure but elude discovery through the fact that the native be kindly dispose to he out of regard for he father 's memory later when caesar have start for italy and only a small army be leave behind in baetica he be join both by the native inhabitant and by those who escape from the battle and with they he come again into baetica because he think it more suitable for the carry on of war there he gain possession of soldier and city particularly after caesar 's death some voluntarily and some by violence the commandant in charge of they gaius asinius pollio hold a force that be far from strong he next set out against spanish carthage but since in he absence pollio make a attack and do some damage he return with a large force meet he opponent and route he after that the follow accident enable he to startle and conquer the rest as well who be contend fiercely pollio have cast off he general 's cloak in order to suffer less chance of detection in he flight and another man of the same name a brilliant horseman have fall the soldier hear the name of the latter who be lie there and see the garment which have be capture be deceive and think that they general have perish surrender in this way sextus conquer and hold possession of nearly that entire region when he be now a powerful factor lepidus arrive to govern the adjoining portion of spain and persuade he to enter into a agreement on condition that he should recover he father 's estate antony influence by he friendship for lepidus and by he hostility toward caesar cause such a decree to be pass so sextus in this way and on these condition hold aloof from spain proper -lrb- -11 - -rrb- caesar and antony in all they act oppose each other but have not fall out openly and whereas in reality they be alienate they try to disguise the fact so far as appearance go as a result all other interest in the city be in a most undecided state and condition of turmoil people be still at peace and yet already at war liberty lead but a shadow existence and the deed do be the deed of royalty to a casual observer antony since he hold the consulship seem to be get the best of it but the enthusiasm of the mass be for caesar this be partly on he father 's account partly on account of the hope he hold out to they but above all because they be displeased at the considerable power of antony and be incline to assist caesar while he be yet devoid of strength neither man have they affection but they be always eager for a change of administration and it be they nature to try to overthrow every superior force and to help any party that be be oppressed consequently they make use of the two to suit they own desire after they have at this period humble antony through the instrumentality of caesar they next undertake to destroy the latter also they irritation toward the man temporarily in power and they liking for the weaker side make they attempt to overthrow the former later they become estrange from the weaker also thus they show dislike for each of they in turn and the same man experience they affection and they hatred they support and they active opposition -lrb- -12 - -rrb- while they be maintain the above attitude toward caesar and antony the war begin as follow antony have set out for brundusium to meet the soldier who have cross over from macedonia caesar send some person to that city with money who be to arrive there before antony and win over the man and himself go to campanium where he collect a large crowd of man chiefly from capua because the people there have receive they land and city from he father whom he say he be avenge he make they many promise and give they on the spot five hundred denarius apiece these man usually constitute the corps of evocatus whom one might term in greek the recall because have end they service they have be recall to it again caesar take charge of they hasten to rome before antony could make he way back and come before the people who have be make ready for he by cannutius there he call to they mind in detail all the excellent work he father have do make a considerable though moderate defense of himself and bring accusation against antony he also praise the soldier who have accompany he say that they be present voluntarily to lend aid to the city that they have elect he to preside over the state and that through he mouth they make know these fact to all for this speech he receive the approbation of he follow and of the throng that stand by after which he depart for etrurium with a view to obtain a accession to he force from that country -lrb- -13 - -rrb- while he be do this antony have be at first kindly receive in brundusium by the soldier because they expect they would secure more from he than be offer they by caesar this belief be base on the idea that he have possession of much more than he rival when however he promise to give each of they a hundred denarius they raise a outcry but he reduce they to submission by order centurion as well as other to be slay before the eye of himself and he wife for the time be the soldier be quiet but on the way toward gaul when they arrive opposite the capital they revolt and many of they despise the lieutenant that have be set over they array themselves on caesar 's side the so-called martian and the fourth legion go over to he in a body he take charge of they and win they attachment by give money to all alike -- a act which add many more to he troops he also capture all the elephant of antony by confront the train suddenly as they be be conduct along antony stop in rome only long enough to arrange a few affair and to bind by oath all the rest of the soldier and the senator who be in they company then he set out for gaul fear that that country too might indulge in a uprising caesar without delay follow behind he -lrb- -14 - -rrb- decimus brutus be at this time governor of that province and antony set great hope upon he because he have be a slayer of caesar but it turn out as follow decimus do not look askance particularly at caesar for the latter have utter no threat against the assassin : on the other hand he see that antony be no more formidable a foe than he rival or indeed than himself or any of the rest who be in power as a result of natural acquisitiveness therefore he refuse to give ground before he caesar when he hear this decision be for some time at a loss what course to adopt the young man hate both decimus and antony but see no way in which he could contend against they both at once he be by no means yet a match for either one of the two and he be further afraid that if he risk such a move he should throw they into each other 's arm and face the unite opposition of the two after stop to reflect that the struggle with antony be already begin and be urgent but that it be not yet a fitting season for take vengeance for he father he decide to make a friend of decimus he understand well that he should find no great difficulty in fight against the latter if with he aid he could first overcome he adversary but that antony would be a powerful antagonist on any subsequent occasion so much do they differ from each other -lrb- -15 - -rrb- accordingly he send a messenger to decimus propose friendship and promising alliance if he would refuse to receive antony this proposal cause the people in the city likewise to join in express they gratitude to caesar just at this time the year be draw to a close and no consul be on the ground dolabellum have be previously send by antony to syrium eulogy however be deliver in the senate by the member themselves and by the soldier who have abandon antony -- with the concurrence also of the tribune when they enter upon the new year they decide in order that they might discuss freely exist condition to employ a guard of soldier at they meeting this pleased nearly all who be in rome at the time -- for they cordially detest antony -- but particularly cicero he on account of he bitter and long-standing hostility toward the man pay court to caesar and so far as he could by speech and action strive to assist he in every way and to injure antony it be for this reason that when he have leave the city to escort he son to athen for the benefit of he education he have return on ascertain that the two be publicly estrange -lrb- -16 - -rrb- besides these event which take place that year servilius isauricus die at a very advanced age i have mention he both for that fact and to show how the roman of that period respect man who be prominent through merit and hate those who behave insolently even on the very slightest grounds this servilius while walk have once meet on the road a man on horseback who so far from dismount on he approach spurn he violently aside later he recognize the fellow in a defendant of a case in court and when he mention the affair to the judge they pay no further attention to the man 's plea but unanimously condemn he -lrb- bc 43 -lrb- _ a u _ 711 -rrb- -rrb- -lrb- -17 - -rrb- in the consulship of aldus hirtius -lrb- who be now appoint consul in spite of the fact that he father 's name have be post on the tablet of sullum -rrb- with he colleague gaius vibius a meeting of the senate be hold and vote be take for three successive day include the first of the month itself as a result of the war which be upon they and the portent very numerous and extremely unfavorable which take place they be so excited that they fail to pass over these _ die nefasti _ on which they ought not to deliberate on any matter touch they interest ominous have be the fall of great number of thunderbolt some of which descend on the shrine sacred to capitoline jupiter that stand in the temple of victory also a great wind arise which snap and scatter the column erect about the temple of saturn and the shrine of fide and likewise knock down and shatter the statue of minerva the protectress which cicero have set up on the capitol before he exile this the temple of vesta leap up after the ceremony in addition to these clear indication of danger a flash dart across from the place of the rise sun to the place of its setting and a new star be see for several day then the light of the sun seem to be diminish and even extinguish and at time to appear in three circle one of which be surmount by a fiery crown of sheaf this if anything prove as clear a sign as possible to they for three man be in power -- i mean caesar and lepidus and antony -- and of they caesar subsequently secure the victory at the same time that these thing occur all sort of plague spread over nearly the whole of italy in a malignant form and in view of this the senate vote that the curia hostilium -lrb- 7 -rrb- should be rebuild and the spot where the naval battle have suddenly fall down and die because of these event many man in the course of those day take one side or the other in they speech and advice and among the deliverance be the following of cicero : -- -lrb- -18 - -rrb- you have hear recently conscript father when i make a statement to you about the matter why i make preparation for my departure as if i be go to be absent from the city a very long time and then return rapidly with the idea that i could benefit you greatly i would not endure a existence under a sovereignty or a tyranny since under such form of government i can not enjoy the rights of free -lrb- 8 -rrb- citizenship nor speak my mind safely nor die in a way that be of service to you and again if opportunity be afford to obey any of duty 's call i would not shrink from action though it involve danger i deem it the task of a upright man equally to keep watch over himself for he country 's interest -lrb- guard himself that he may not perish uselessly -rrb- and in this course of action not to fail to say or do whatever be requisite even if it be necessary to suffer some harm in preserve he native land -lrb- -19 - -rrb- these assumption grant a large degree of safety be afford by caesar both to you and to I for the discussion of press question and since you have further vote to assemble under guard we must frame all we word and behavior this day in such a fashion as to establish the present state of affair and provide for the future that we may not again be compel to decide in a similar way about it that we condition be difficult and dangerous and require much care and attention you yourselve have make evident if in no other way at least by this measure for you would not have vote to keep the senate-house under guard if it have be possible for you to deliberate at all with you accustomed orderliness and in quiet free from fear it be necessary for we even on account of the presence of the soldier to accomplish some measure of importance that we may not incur the disgrace that would certainly follow from ask for they as if we fear somebody and then neglect affair as if we be liable to no danger we shall appear to have acquire they only nominally in behalf of the city against antony but to have give they in reality to he against we own self and it will look as if in addition to the other legion which he gather against he country he need to acquire these very man and so prevent you pass any vote against he even to-day -lrb- -20 - -rrb- yet some have attain such a height of shamelessness as to dare to say that he be not war against the state and have credit you with so great folly as to think that they will persuade you to attend to they word rather than to he act but who would choose to desist from regard he performance and the campaign which he have make against we ally without any order from the senate or the people the country which he be overrun the city which he be besiege and the hope upon which he be build in he entire course -- who would distrust i say the evidence of he own eye and to he ruin yield credence to the word of these man and they false statement by which they put you off with pretext and excuse i myself be far from assert that in do this he be carry out any legal act of administration on the contrary because he have abandon the province of macedonium which be assign to he by lot and because he choose instead the province of gaul which in no way pertain to he and because he assume control of the legion which caesar have send ahead against the parthian keep they about he though no danger threaten italy and because he have leave the city during the period of he consulship to go about pillage and injure the country -- for all these reason i declare that he have long be a enemy of we all -lrb- -21 - -rrb- if you do not perceive it immediately at the start or experience vexation at each of he action he deserve to be hate all the more on this account in that he do not cease injure you who be so long-suffering he might perchance have obtain pardon for the error which he commit at first but now by he perseverance in evil he have reach such a pitch of knavery that he ought to be bring to book for he former offence as well and you ought to be especially careful in regard to the situation notice and consider this point -- that the man who have so often despise you in such weighty matter can not submit to be correct by the same gentleness and kindliness that you have show but must now against he will even though never previously be chastise by force of arm and because he partly persuade and partly compel you to vote he some privilege do not think that this make he less guilty or deserving of less punishment quite the reverse -- for this very procedure in particular he merit the infliction of a penalty : he determine from the outset to commit many outrage and after accomplish some of they through you he employ against you own self the resource which come from you which by deception he force you to vote to he though you neither know nor foresee any such result on what occasion do you voluntarily abolish the command give by caesar or by the lot to each man and allow this person to distribute many appointment to he friend and companion send he brother gaius to macedonia and assign gaul to himself with the aid of the legion which he be not by any means keep to use in you defense do you not remember how when he find you startle at caesar 's demise he carry out all the plan that he choose communicate some to you carefully dissimulate and at inopportune moment and on he own responsibility execute other that inflict injury while all he act be characterize by violence he use soldier and barbarian at that against you and need any one be surprise that in those day some vote be pass which should not have be when even now we have not obtain a free hand to speak and do what be requisite in any other way than by the aid of a body-guard if we have be formerly endue with this power he would not have obtain what any one may say he have obtain nor would he have rise to the prominence enable he to do the deed that be a natural sequence accordingly let no one retort that the rights which we be see to give he under command and compulsion and amid lament be legally and rightfully bestow for even in private business that be not consider binding which a man do under compulsion from another -lrb- -23 - -rrb- and yet all these measure which you be see to have vote you will find to be slight and vary but little from establish custom what be there dreadful in the fact that one man be destine to govern macedonium or gaul in place of another or what be the harm if a man obtain soldier during he consulship but these be the fact that be harmful and abominable -- that you land should be damage ally city besiege that we soldier should be arm against we and we means expend to we detriment : this you neither vote nor intend do not merely because you have grant he some privilege allow he to usurp what be not grant he and do not think that just as you have concede some point he ought similarly to be permit to do what have not be concede quite the reverse : you should for this very reason both hate and punish he because he have dare not only in this case but in all other case to use the honor and kindness that you bestow against you look at the matter through my influence you vote that there should be peace and harmony between individual this man be order to manage the business and conduct it in such a way -lrb- take caesar 's funeral as a pretext -rrb- that almost the whole city be burn down and great number be once more slaughter you ratify all the grant make to various person and all the law lay down by caesar not because they be all excellent -- far from it -- but because we mutual and unsuspecting association quite free from any disguise be not further by change any one of those enactment this man appoint to examine into they have abolish many of he act and have substitute many other in the document he have take away land and citizenship and exemption from tax and many other honor from the possessor -- private individual king and city -- and have give they to man who have not receive any alter the memorandum of caesar from those who be unwilling to give up anything to he grasp he take away even what have be give they and sell this and everything else to such as wish to buy yet you foresee this very possibility have vote that no tablet should be set up after caesar 's death which might contain any article give by declare that we ought not yet to make a enemy of either of these man in arm nor to enquire exactly what they have be do or in what way the present crisis be not suitable for this action and as they be all alike we fellow-citizen if any one of they fail the loss will be ours or if any one of they succeed he aggrandizement will be a menace to we wherefore i believe that we ought to treat they as friend and citizen and send messenger to all of they alike bid they lay down they arm and put themselves and they legion in we hand and that we ought not yet to wage war on any one of they but after they reply have come back approve those who be willing to obey we and fight against the disobedient this course be just and expedient for we -- not to be in a hurry or do anything rashly but to wait and after give the leader themselves and they soldier a opportunity to change they mind then if in such case there be need of war to give the consul charge of it -lrb- -28 - -rrb- and you cicero i promoter of friendship among we then destroy it remember that day and the speech which you deliver in the precinct of tellus and yield a little to this goddess of concord under whose guidance we be now deliberate and avoid discrediting those statement and make they appear as if not utter from a sincere heart or by somebody else on that occasion this be to the advantage of the state and will bring you most renown do not think that audacity be either glorious or safe and do not feel sure of be praise just for say that you despise death such man all suspect and hate as be likely to venture some deed of evil through desperation those whom they see however pay greatest attention to they own safety they praise and laud because such would not willingly do anything that merit death do you therefore if you honestly wish you country to be safe speak and act in such a way as will both preserve yourself and not by jupiter involve we in you destruction -lrb- -29 - -rrb- such language from fortification the sacrifice of purification which regularly precede struggle hence they urge a battle and spread a report that if there should be more delay they would abandon the camp and disperse and at this the leader though against they will go to meet the foe -lrb- -39 - -rrb- you might not unnaturally guess that this struggle prove tremendous and surpass all previous civil conflict of the roman this be not because these contestant excel those of the old day in either the number or the valor of the warrior for far larger mass and braver man than they have fight on many field but because on this occasion they contend for liberty and for democracy as never before and they come to blow with one another again later just as they have previously but the subsequent struggle they carry on to see to whom they should belong : on this occasion the one side be try to bring they into subjection to sovereignty the other side into a state of autonomy hence the people never attain again to the absolute right of free speech in spite of be vanquish by no foreign nation -lrb- the subject population and the ally nation then present on both side be merely a kind of complement of the citizen army -rrb- : but the people at once gain the mastery over and fall into subjection to itself it defeat itself and be defeat and in that effort it exhaust the democratic element and strengthen the monarchical i do not say that the people 's defeat at that time be not beneficial -lrb- what else can one say regard those who fight on both side than that the roman be conquer and caesar be victorious -rrb- they be no longer capable of concord in the established form of government for it be impossible for a unadulterated democracy that have grow to acquire domain of such vast size to have the faculty of moderation after undertake many similar conflict repeatedly one after another they would certainly some day have be either enslave or ruin -lrb- -40 - -rrb- we may infer also from the portent which appear to they on that occasion that the struggle between they be clearly tremendous heaven as it be ever accustom to give indication before most remarkable event foretell to they accurately both in rome and in macedonium all the result that would come from it in the city the sun at one time appear diminish and grow extremely small and again show itself now huge now triple in form and once shine forth at night thunderbolt descend on many spot and most significantly upon the altar of jupiter victor flash dart hither and thither note of trumpet clashing of arm and cry of camp be hear by night from the garden of caesar and of antony located close together beside the tiber moreover a dog drag the body of a dog to the temple of cere where he dig the earth with he paw and bury it a child be bear with hand that have ten finger and a mule give birth to a prodigy of two species the front part of it resemble a horse and the rest a mule the chariot of minerva while return to the capitol from a horse-race be dash to piece and the statue of jupiter at albanum send forth blood at the very time of the feria from its right shoulder and right hand these be advance indication to they from heaven and the river also in they land give out entirely or begin to flow backward and any chance deed of man seem to point to the same end during the feriae the prefect of the city sextus through companion as to how and on what term they could effect a reconciliation afterward the party concern hold a conference near misenum the two from the capital take they stand on the land the other on a kind of mound construct for he safety in the sea by which it be purposely surround not far from they there be also present the entire fleet of sextus and the entire infantry force of the other two and not that merely but the one command have be draw up on the shore and the other on the ship both fully arm so that this very fact make it perfectly evident to all that it be from fear of they accoutrement and from necessity that the two ruler be make peace because of the people and sextus because of he adherent the compact be frame upon the following condition -- that the deserter from among the slave should be free and that all those drive out save the assassin should be restore the latter of course they have to exclude but in reality several of they be destine to return sextus himself indeed be think to have be one of they it be record at any rate that all the rest save those mention should be allow to return under a general amnesty and with a right to a quarter of they confiscate property that tribuneship praetorship and priesthood should be give to some of they immediately that sextus himself should be choose consul and be appoint augur should obtain seventeen hundred and fifty myriad of denarius from he paternal estate and should govern sicily sardinia and achaea for five year not receive deserter nor acquire more ship nor keep any garrison in italy but bend he effort to secure peace on the sea for the peninsula and send a state amount of grain to the people of the city they limit he to this period of time because they wish it to appear that they also be hold merely a temporary and not a unending authority -lrb- -37 - -rrb- after settle and draft these compact they deposit the document with the priestess -- the vestal virgin -- and then exchange pledge and treat one another as friend upon this a tremendous and inextinguishable shout arise from the mainland and the ship at once for many soldier and many individual who be present suddenly utter a cry in unison because they be terribly tired of the war and vehemently desire peace and the mountain resound so that great panic and alarm be spread and many die of fright at the very reverberation while other perish by be trample under foot and suffocate those who be in the small boat do not wait to reach the land itself but jump out into the sea and the rest rush out into the breaker meantime they embrace one another while swimming and throw they arm around one another 's neck under water make a diversified picture accompany by diversified sound some know that they relative and associate be live and see they present give way to unrestrained joy other think that those dear to they have die previously see they now unexpectedly and for a long time know not what to do but be render speechless distrust they sight yet pray that it might be true and they be not sure of they until they have call they name and have hear they say something they rejoice as if the man have be bring to life again but as they be force to share they pleasure with a multitude they do not continue without tear again some who be unaware that they loved one have perish and think they be alive and present seek for they and go about ask every one they meet regard they as long as they could learn nothing they be like maniac and be tear different way both hope to find they and fear that they be dead -- not able to despair in view of they desire nor to indulge in grief in view of they hope on learn at last the truth they would tear they hair and rend they clothing call upon the lose by name as if they could hear anything and give way to grief as if they friend be just dead and lie there somewhere and if any of they be affect in no such way they be at least disturb by the experience of the rest they either rejoice with somebody in joy or grieve with somebody in pain and so even if they be free from personal interest yet they could not remain indifferent on account of they connection with the rest as a result there be no possibility of they be either sate or ashamed because they be all affect in the same way and they spend the entire day as well as the greater part of the night in this behavior -lrb- -38 - -rrb- after this the party chiefly concern as well as the rest receive one another and inaugurate entertainment in turn first sextus on the ship and then caesar and antony on the shore sextus so far surpass they in power that he would not disembark to meet they on the mainland until they have go aboard he boat in the course of this proceeding however he refuse to murder they both in the small boat with only a few follower though he might easily have do so and mena advise it -lrb- 47 -rrb- to antony who have possession of he ancestral home at -39 - -rrb- this war then have be defer : that of labienus and the parthian come to a end in the following way antony himself return from italy to greece and delay there a very long time satisfy he phranapate lieutenant of pacorus who be guard the passage and that would have be he fate have not ventidius by chance come upon he when he be fight and defend he he attack the barbarian who be not however obtain praise and thanksgiving as for the aradius they be afraid that they might have to pay the penalty for what they have venture against antony and would not come to term though they be besiege by he for a time later they be with difficulty capture by other -lrb- -40 - -rrb- about this same time a uprising take place in parthian illyricum but be put down by pollio after some conflict lieutenant who be ambuscade by the barbarian and desert by he soldier they leader undertake no operation against the enemy until he have punish they call they together as if for some other purpose he as many other after do this and gain like marcus crassus a renown for he discipline the army he set out against he opponent and with no great difficulty vanquish they he obtain a triumph in spite of rivalry attack mena and perish make the loss of sextus a equal one for this reason the latter lay no claim to victory and caesar console himself over the defeat -lrb- -47 - -rrb- he happen at this scyllaeum the italian promontory without trouble but as he be round that point a great wind fall upon he hurl some of the ship against the promontory sink other out at sea and scatter all the rest sextus on ascertain this send the fleet under command of apollophane against they he discover caesar coast along somewhere in these part with the intention of cross into sicily along with sabinus make a dash upon he caesar have the ship come to anchor marshal the heavy-armed soldier upon they and at first make a noble resistance the ship be draw up with prow face outward and so offer no safe point for attack but be shorter and higher could do more hurt to those that approach they and the heavy-armed fighter when they could come in conflict with the enemy prove far superior apollophane however transfer such as be wound and be in difficulty from time to time to other ship assign for the purpose by back water and take on board fresh man he also make constant charge and use missile carry fire so that he adversary be at last route flee to the land and come to anchor when even then the pursuer press he hard some of caesar 's ship suddenly cut they anchor and unexpectedly offer opposition it be only this and the fact that night interrupted operation that keep apollophane from burn some of the ship and tow all the rest away -lrb- -48 - -rrb- after this event a ill-fated wind on the follow day fall upon caesar and sabinus as they be anchor together and make they previous reverse seem small the fleet of sabinus suffer the less for mena be a old hand on the sea foresee the storm he immediately station he ship out at sea let they ride with slack anchor some distance apart so that the rope should not be stretch and break then he row directly against the wind and in this way no rope be strain and he remain constantly in the same position recover by the use of the oar all the distance which he lose by the impetus of the wind the remain commander because they have go through a severe experience the day before and as yet have no precise knowledge of nautical matter be cast out upon the shore close by and lose many ship the night which have be of the greatest aid to they before be now among the chief agency in promote disaster all through it the wind blow violently tear the vessel from they anchor and dash they against the rock that of course be the end of they and the sailor and marine likewise perish without hope of rescue since the darkness prevent they from see ahead and they could not hear a word because of the uproar and the reverberation from the mountain especially since the wind smite they in the face so it be that caesar despaired of sicily and be satisfy to guard the coast country : sextus on the other hand be still more elated believe himself in very truth to be the son of neptune and he put on a dark blue robe besides as some relate cast horse as well as man alive into the strait he plunder and harass italy himself send apollophane to libya the latter be pursue by mena who overtake and injure he the island round about sicily go over to the side of sextus whereupon caesar seize the territory of the liparean in advance and eject they from the island convey they to campanium where he force they to live in neapoli so long as the war should continue -lrb- -49 - -rrb- meantime he keep have boat make throughout almost all of italy and collect slave for rower first from he friend who be suppose to give willingly and then from the rest -- senator and knight and well-to-do private citizen he also assemble heavy-armed troops and gather money from all citizen ally and subject both in italy and abroad this year and the follow he spend on the construction of ship and the gathering and training of rower -lrb- bc 37 -lrb- _ a u _ 717 -rrb- -rrb- he himself oversee and arrange these detail and all other matter in italy and in gaul -lrb- where there be a slight uprising -rrb- to agrippa he entrust the equipment of the boat he send those day without harbor -- he conceive and execute a magnificent enterprise which i shall describe at some length show its nature and the present characteristic of the locality where it take place -lrb- -50 - -rrb- at cyme in campanium between misenum and puteolus there be a crescent-shaped spot it be shut in by small hill bare except in a few place and the sea there form a kind of triple bay the first be outside and near the city the second be separate from it by a small passage and the third like a real harbor be see far back the last name be call avernus and the middle bay lucrinus : the outer one belong to the tyrrhenian sea and take its name from that water in this roadstead within the other two which have but narrow entrance then agrippa by cut channel close along the shore through the land separate lucrinus from the sea on each side produce harbor afford most safe anchorage for ship while the man be work a certain image situate above avernus either of calypso to whom this place whither they say odysseus also sail be devoted or to some other heroine be cover with sweat like a human body -lrb- -51 - -rrb- now what this import i can not say but i will go on to tell of everything else worth report which i saw in that place these mountain close to the inner body of water have spring full of both fire and water in considerable quantity mix together neither of the two element be anywhere to be find by itself -lrb- that be neither pure fire or cold water alone be to be see -rrb- but from they association the water be heated and the fire moisten the former on its way down the foothill to the sea run into reservoir and the inhabitant conduct the steam from it through pipe into room set up high where they use the steam for vapor bath the higher it ascend from the earth and from the water the dryer it become costly apparatus have be install for turn both the fire and the vapor to practical use and they be very well suit for employment in the conduct of daily life and also for effect cure now besides these product that mountain make a earth the peculiar nature of which i be go to describe since the fire have not the power of burning -lrb- for by its union with the water all its blaze quality be extinguish -rrb- but be still able to separate and melt the substance with which it come in contact it follow that the oily part of the earth be melt by it whereas the hard and what i might call the bony part of it be leave as it be hence the mass of earth necessarily become porous and when expose to the dry air crumble into dust but when they be place in a swirl of water and sand grow into a solid piece as much of they as be in the liquid harden and petrify the reason for this be that the brittle element in they be disintegrate and break up by the fire which possess the same nature but by the admixture of dampness be chill and so be compress all over through and through become indissoluble such be baiae where agrippa as soon as he have construct the entrance collect ship and rower of which he fortify the former with armor and train the latter to row on wooden bench -lrb- -52 - -rrb- now the population of rome be be disturb by sign among the various piece of news bring to they be one to the effect that many dolphin battle with one another and perish near aspis the african city and in the vicinity of the city blood descend from heaven and be smear all about by the bird when at the ludus romanus not one of the senator be entertain on the capitol as have be the custom they take this too as a portent again the incident that happen to livium cause she pleasure but inspire the rest with terror a white bird carry a sprig of fruited laurel have be throw by a eagle into she lap as this seem to be a sign of no small importance she take care of the bird and plant the laurel the latter take root and grow so that it amply supply those who be afterward to celebrate triumph and livium be destine to hold caesar 's power in a fold of she robe and to dominate he in everything -lrb- -53 - -rrb- the rest however in the city have they peace of mind thoroughly shatter by this and the difference between official not only the consul and praetor but even the quaestor be array against one another and this last for some time the reason be that all be anxious not so much to hold office a longer time at home as to be count among the ex-official and secure the outward honor and influence that belong to that class they be no longer choose for any specified time but take just long enough to enter upon the title of the office and resign whenever it so seem good to those in power many do both on the same day some actually have to abandon hope of office through poverty and in this i be not speak of those then support sextus who have be disenfranchise as if by some principle of right but we have the case of a certain marcus oppius who through lack of means desire to resign the aedileship -- both he and he father have be among the proscribe -- and the populace would not permit it but contribute money for he various necessity of life and the expense of he office and the story go that some criminal too really come into the theater in mask as if they be actor and leave they money there with the rest so this man be love by the multitude while in life and at he death not long after be carry to the campus martius and there burn and bury the senate be indignant at the utter devotion of the mass to he and take up he bone on the plea that it be impious for they to lie in that consecrated spot they be persuade by the pontifice to make this declaration although they bury many other man there both before and after -lrb- -54 - -rrb- at this same period antony come into italy again from syrium the reason he give be that he intend to bear he share of the war against sextus because of caesar 's mishap he do not however stay by he colleague but have come to spy upon he action rather than to accomplish anything he give he some ship and promise to send other in return for which he receive heavy-armed infantry and set sail himself state that he be go to conduct a campaign against the parthian before he depart they present to each other they mutual grievance at first through friend and then personally as they have no leisure for war together they become reconcile in a way chiefly through the instrumentality the exist situation furthermore antony send octavium herself at once from corcyra to italy that she might not share he danger while he be war against the parthian besides the above negotiation at that further vex because he hold no office but have be make a subordinate of sabinus desert again to sextus dio 's roman history 49 the following be contain in the forty-ninth of dio 's rome how caesar -1 - -rrb- this happen in the winter when lucius gellius and cocceius nerva become consul caesar when he fleet have be make ready and spring set in start from baise and coast along italy have great hope of encompass sicily on all side for he be sail thither with many ship and those of antony be already in the strait also lepidus though reluctantly have promise to assist he he greatest ground of confidence lay in the height of the vessel and the thickness of the timber they have be build unusually stout and unusually high so as to carry the largest number of marine possible indeed they be collision more violent with such calculation caesar be hasten to sicily as he be pass the promontory of palinurus so-called a great storm fall upon he this destroy many ship and mena come upon the lepidus and be under suspicion in nearly every way caesar be then extremely glad to receive he but trust he no longer he first repair the damaged ship free the slave that serve on the trireme and there agrippa and the ship return to the mainland with the intention of transport the infantry across into sicily when a opportunity should arise -lrb- -2 - -rrb- on learn this sextus himself lay they be strike from the tower in the combat and bring alongside by grapple iron they suffer no less harm than they inflict the caesarian also when they come into close conflict and have cross over to the hostile ship prove superior but as the enemy leap out into the sea whenever the boat sink and by they swimming well and be lightly equipped succeed easily in climb upon other the attacker be at a corresponding disadvantage meantime the rapidity with which the ship of the one party could sail prove a offset to the solidity of those on the other side and the heaviness of the latter counterbalance the agility of the former -lrb- -4 - -rrb- late in the day near nightfall caesar 's party finally conquer but institute no pursuit : the reason as it appear to I and may be conjecture from probability be that they could not overtake the flee ship and be afraid of run aground in the shallows with which they be unacquainted near the coast some say that agrippa because he be battle for caesar and not for himself think it sufficient merely to rout he adversary for he have be in the habit of say to he most intimate associate that the majority of those hold sovereign power wish no one to display more ability than themselves and that they attend personally to nearly all such matter as afford they a conquest without effort but assign the less favorable and more complicated business to other and if they ever be force to entrust some choice enterprise to they assistant they be irritated and displeased at the latter 's renown they do not pray that these subordinate may be defeat and fare badly yet they do not choose to have they win a complete success and secure glory from it he advice therefore be that the man who intend to survive must relieve he master of the annoyance incident to such undertaking and still reserve for they the successful completion of the work as for I i know that the above be regularly true and that agrippa pay attention to it but i be not set down that on that particular occasion this be the cause of he failure to pursue for he be not able no matter how much he might have desire it to follow up the foe -lrb- -5 - -rrb- while the and betake themselves to various place some go to antony among whom be monaese this happen in the consulship of agrippa and gallus -lrb- bc 36 -lrb- _ a u _ 718 -rrb- -rrb- -lrb- -24 - -rrb- during the remainder of winter when gallus and nerva be hold office publius canidius crassus make a campaign against the iberian that inhabit this portion of the world conquer in battle they king pharnabazus and bring they into alliance with this king he invade albanis the adjoining country and after overcome the dweller there and they king zober conciliate they likewise antony be elate at this and 's stronghold at one blow he assail praaspa the royal residence heap up mound and make constant attack when the parthian and the medan king ascertain this they leave he to continue he idle toil -- for the wall be strong and many be defend they -- but assail statianus off he guard and weary on the march and slew the whole detachment except polemon king of pontus who be then accompany the expedition he alone they take alive and release in exchange for ransom they be able to accomplish this because the armenian king be not present at the battle but though he might have help the roman as some say he neither do this nor join antony but retire to he own country -lrb- -26 - -rrb- antony hasten at the first message send he by statianus to go to he assistance but be too late for except corpse he find no one this outcome cause he fear but inasmuch as he fall in with no barbarian he suspect that they have depart in some direction through terror and this lend he new courage hence when he meet they a little later he route they for he slinger be numerous and as the latter could shoot farther than would the bow they inflict severe injury upon the man in armor however he do not kill any remarkable number of they because the barbarian could ride fast so he proceed again against praaspa and besiege it though he do no great damage to the enemy for the man inside the wall repulse he vigorously and those outside could not easily be entrap into a combat thus he lose many of he own man in search for and bring provision and many by he own discipline at first as long as they could get they food from somewhere in the neighborhood they have no difficulty about either undertaking : they could attend to the siege and safely secure supplies both at once when however all material at hand have be use up and the soldier be oblige to go to some distance it happen to they that if few be send anywhere not only do they not bring anything but they perish as well if a number be send they leave the wall destitute of besieger and meantime lose many man and many engine at the hand of the barbarian who would make a sortie against they -lrb- -27 - -rrb- for this reason antony give they all barley instead of wheat and destroy every tenth man in some instance : indeed the entire force which be suppose to be besiege endure the hardship of person besiege the man within the wall watch carefully for opportunity to make sally and those outside harass fearfully the roman that remain in position as often as they become separated accomplish this by make a sudden charge and wheeling about again in a narrow space : this force outside do not trouble the food train while the latter be en route to the village but would fall upon they unexpectedly when scatter in the homeward march previously post so that many perish through such mishap and many of hunger -lrb- -29 - -rrb- as a result there be some desertion and they would all have go over have not the barbarian shoot down before the eye of the other any who dare to take this course consequently the man refrain from this and from fortune 's hand obtain the follow relief one day when they fall into a ambush and be strike with fast-flying arrow they suddenly make by join shield the _ testudo _ and rest they leave knee on the ground the barbarian have never see anything of the kind before and think that they have fall from they wound and need only one finish blow so they throw aside they bow leap from they horse and draw they dagger come close to put a end to they at this the roman rise to they foot spread out the phalanx at a word and each one attack the man nearest and face he thus they cut down great number since they be contend arm against a unprotected foe man prepare against man off they guard heavy infantry against archer roman against barbarian all the survivor immediately retire and no one follow they for the future -lrb- -30 - -rrb- this _ testudo _ and the way in which it be form deserve a word of explanation the baggage animal the light-armed troops and the cavalry be marshal in the center of the army those infantryman who use the oblong hollow grooved shield be draw up around the edge make a rectangular figure and face outward with spear-point project -lrb- 52 -rrb- they enclose the rest the other infantryman who have flat shield form a compact body in the center and raise they shield above themselves and above all the rest so that nothing but shield can be see in every part of the phalanx alike and all the man by the density of formation be under shelter from missile it be so marvelously strong that man can walk upon it and when ever they get into a hollow narrow passage even horse and vehicle can be drive over it such be the method of this arrangement and this show why it have receive the title of _ testudo _ -lrb- 53 -rrb- -- with reference to its strength and to the excellent shelter it afford they use it in two way : either they approach some fort to assault it often even enable man to scale the very wall or where sometimes they be surround by archer they all bend together -- even the horse be teach to kneel and recline -- and thereby cause the foe to think that they be exhaust then when the other draw near they suddenly rise to the latter 's great alarm -lrb- -31 - -rrb- the _ testudo _ then be the kind of device just describe as for antony he suffer no a man who choose the less just of two course might expect to win with its aid nevertheless i base my confidence far more upon the cause underlie the war than upon this factor for that we who be roman and lord of the greatest and best portion of the world should be despise and trodden under foot of a egyptian woman be unworthy of we father who overthrow pyrrhus philip perseus antiochus who uproot the numantinus and the carthaginian who cut down the cimbrus and the ambrone it be unworthy also of ourselves who have subjugate the gaul have subdue the pannonian have advance as far as the ister have cross the rhine have go over into britain how could all those who have have a hand in the exploit mention fail to grieve vehemently if they should learn that we have succumb to a accursed woman should we not be guilty of a gross deviation from right conduct if after surpass all man everywhere in valor we should then bear humbly the insult of this throng who o hercule be alexandrian and egyptian -lrb- what worse or what truer name could one apply to they -rrb- who serve reptile and other creature as god who embalm they body to secure a reputation for immortality who be most reckless in braggadocio but most deficient in bravery and worst of all be slave to a woman instead of a man yet these have dare to lay claim to we possession and to acquire they through we evidently expect that we will give up the prosperity which we possess for they -lrb- -25 - -rrb- who can help lament to see roman soldier act as body-guard of they queen who can help groan when he hear roman knight and senator flattering she like eunuch who can help weep when he both hear and see antony himself the man twice consul often imperator to whom be commit in common with I the superintendence of the public business who be entrust with so many city so many legion -- when he see that this man have now abandon all he ancestor ' habit of life have emulate all alien and barbaric custom that he pay no honor to we or to the law or to he father ' god but worship that wench as if she be some isis or selene call she child sun and moon and finally himself bear the title of osiri and dionysus in consequence of which he have bestow entire island and some of the continent as though he be master of the whole earth and the whole sea i be sure that this appear marvelous and incredible to you fellow-soldier : therefore you ought to be the more indignant for if that be actually so which you do not even believe on hear it and if that man in he voluptuary career commit act at which any one who learn of they must grieve would you not properly become exceedingly enraged -lrb- -26 - -rrb- yet at the start i be so devoted to he that i give he a share of my leadership marry my sister to he and grant he legion even after this i feel so kindly so affectionately toward he that i be unwilling to wage war on he because of he insulting my sister or because he neglect the child she have bear he or because he prefer the egyptian woman to she or because he bestow upon the former 's child practically all you possession or in fine for any other reason the cause be that first of all i do not think it proper to assume the same attitude toward antony as toward cleopatra i deem she by the very fact of she foreign birth to be at the outset hostile to he career but i believe that he as a citizen could be correct later i entertain the hope that if not voluntarily at least reluctantly he might change he mind as a result of the decree pass against she consequently i do not declare war upon he he however have look haughtily and disdainfully upon my effort and will neither be release though we would fain release he nor be pity though we try to pity he he be either unreasonable or mad -- and this which i have hear i do believe that he have be bewitch by that accursed female -- and therefore pay no heed to we kindness or humaneness but be in slavery to that woman he undertake in she behalf both war and needless danger which be both against we interest and against those of he country what else then be we duty except to fight he back together with cleopatra -lrb- -27 - -rrb- hence let no one call he a roman but rather a egyptian nor antony but rather serapio let no one think that he be ever consul or imperator but only gymnasiarch he have himself of he own free will choose the latter title instead of the former and cast away all the August term of he own land have become one of the cymbal player from canopus -lrb- 65 -rrb- again let no one fear that he can give any unfavorable turn to the war even previously he be of no ability as you know clearly who conquer he near mutina and even if once he do attain to some capacity through campaigning with we be well assure that he have now ruin all of it by he changed manner of life it be impossible for one who lead a existence of royal luxury and coddle himself like a woman to think any valorous thought or do valorous deed because it be quite inevitable that a person take the impress of the practice with which he come in contact a proof of this be that in the one war which he have wage in all this long time and the one campaign that he have make he lose great number of citizen in the battle return in thorough disgrace from praaspa and part with very many additional man in the flight if any one of we be oblige to perform a set dance or cordax -lrb- 66 -rrb- in a amusing way such a person would surely yield the honor to he he have practice this : but since it be a case of arm and battle what be there about he that any one should dread he physical condition he have pass he prime and become effeminate he strength of mind he play the woman and have surrender himself to unnatural lust he piety toward we god he be at war both with they and he country he faithfulness to he ally but be any one unaware how he deceive and imprison the armenian he liberal treatment of he friend but who have not see the man who have miserably perish at he hand he reputation with the soldier but who even of they have not condemn he evidence of they feeling be find in the fact that number daily come over to we side for my part i think that all we citizen will do this as on a former occasion when he be go from brundusium into gaul so long as they expect to get rich without danger some be very glad to cleave to he but they will not care to fight against we they own countryman in behalf of what do not belong to they at all especially when they be give the opportunity to win without hazard both preservation and prosperity by join we -lrb- -28 - -rrb- some one may say however that he have many ally and a store of wealth well how we have be accustom to conquer the dweller on asia the mainland be know to scipio asiaticus the renowned be know to sulla the fortunate to lucullus to pompey to my father caesar and to you own self who vanquish the supporter of brutus and cassius this be so if you think they wealth be so much more than other ' you must be all the more eager to make it you own it be but fair that for the greatest prize the greatest conflict should be undergo and i can tell you nothing else greater than that prize which lie within you grasp -- namely to preserve the renown of you forefather to guard you individual pride to take vengeance on those in revolt against we to repulse those who insult you to conquer and rule all mankind to allow no woman to make herself equal to a man against the tauriscus and iapude and dalmatian and pannonian you yourselve now before I battle most zealously and frequently for some few wall and desert land you subdue all of they though they be admittedly a most warlike race and by jupiter against sextus also for sicily merely and against this very antony for mutina merely you carry on a similar struggle so that you come out victorious over both and now will you show any less zeal against a woman whose plot concern all you possession and against she husband who have distribute to she child all you property and against they noble associate and table companion whom they themselves stigmatize as ` privy ' councillor why should you because of they number but no number of person can conquer valor because of they race but they have practice carry burden rather than warfare because of they experience but they know better how to row than how to fight at sea i for my part be really ashamed that we be go to contend with such creature by vanquish whom we shall gain no glory whereas if we be defeat we shall be disgrace -lrb- -29 - -rrb- and surely you must not think that the size of they vessel or the thickness of the timber of they ship be a match for we valor what ship ever by itself either wound or kill anybody will they not by they very height and staunchness be more difficult for they rower to move and less obedient to they pilot of what use can they possibly be to the fight man on board of they when these man can employ neither frontal assault nor flank attack maneuver which you know be essential in naval contest for surely they do not intend to employ infantry tactic against we on the sea nor on the other hand be they prepare to shut themselves up as it be in wooden wall and undergo a siege since that would be decidedly to we advantage -- i mean assault wooden barrier for if they ship remain in the same place as if fasten there it will be possible for we to rip they open with we beak it will be possible too to damage they with we engine from a distance and also possible to burn they to the water 's edge with incendiary missile and if they do venture to stir from they place they will not overtake anyone by pursue nor escape by flee since they be so heavy that they be entirely too inert to inflict any damage and so huge that they be exceptionally liable to suffer it -lrb- -30 - -rrb- indeed what need be there to spend time in speak further of they when we have already often make trial of they not only off leuca but also here just the other day and so far from prove inferior to they we have everywhere show ourselves superior hence you should be encourage not so much by my word as by you own deed and should desire to put a end forthwith to the whole war for be well assure that if we beat they to-day we shall have no further trouble for in general it be a natural characteristic of human nature everywhere that whenever a man fail in he first contest he become dishearten with respect to what be to come and as for we we be so indisputably superior to they on land that we could vanquish they even if they have never suffer any injury and they be themselves so conscious of this truth -- for i be not go to conceal from you what i have hear -- that they be discourage at what have already happen and despair of save they life if they stay where they be and they be therefore endeavor to make they escape to some place or other and be make this sally not with the desire to give battle but in expectation of flight in fact they have place in they ship the best and most valuable of the possession they have with they in order to escape with they if they can since then they admit that they be weaker than we and since they carry the prize of victory in they ship let we not allow they to sail anywhere else but let we conquer they here on the spot and take all these treasure away from they such be caesar 's word -lrb- -31 - -rrb- after this he form a plan to let they slip by intend to fall upon they from the rear : he himself by fast sailing expect to capture they directly and when the 's fleet alone and have create disturbance all through it hence he abandon this plan and after put vast number of infantry aboard the ship himself and place all he associate into auxiliary boat for the purpose of sailing about quickly give notice of requisite action to the warrior and report to he what he ought to know he await the onset of the foe they weigh anchor to the sound of the trumpet and with ship in close array draw up they line a little outside the narrow not advance any farther : he in turn start out as if to come to close quarter or even make they retire when they neither make a corresponding advance nor turn about but remain in position and further make they array extremely dense he become doubtful what to do therefore he order the sailor to let they oar rest in the water of this movement of he to wheel about and surround they and hence adopt so far as he could correspond tactic which bring he though reluctantly into close combat -lrb- -32 - -rrb- so they attack and endeavor to avoid this calamity they would waste time and lay themselves open to attack on the part of some other for when two or three at once fall upon the same ship part would do all the damage they could and the rest suffer the brunt of the injury on the one side the pilot and the rower endure the most annoyance and fatigue and on the other the marine : and the one side resemble cavalry now make a charge now withdraw on account of the maneuver on they part in assault and back water and the other be like heavy-armed man guard against the approach of foe and try as much as possible to hold they as a result they gain mutual advantage : the one party fall unobserved upon the line of oar project from the ship and shatter the blade whereas the other party with rock and engine from above try to sink they there be also certain disadvantage : the one party could not injure those approach it and the other party if it fail to sink some vessel by its ramming be hem in and find no longer a equal contest -lrb- -33 - -rrb- the battle be a even one for a long time and neither antagonist could get the upper hand but the outcome of it be finally like this cleopatra ride at anchor behind the because of fear for macedonium come out to meet they by he mere approach he throw they into a panic and drive they from the land without a conflict next he pursue they as they be retire homeward gain
